  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_97faecb6-3a87-487a-95de-849af1d7f4c0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_1426648591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426648591" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426648591?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340952658" href="/book/show/1020712.Desperation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=stephen-king-read">stephen-king-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426648591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13473989351804289647"><b>**4.5-stars rounded up**</b><br/><br/>A bizarre cast of characters come together to fight an ancient and powerful entity of evil.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473169952ra/20420495.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That would be my single sentence synopsis if someone were to ask me, what is <i>Desperation</i> all about?<br/><br/>If you have ever read a Stephen King novel, however, you are probably aware that the real answer is <b>way more complex</b> than that.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513055371ra/24658928.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I first read <i>Desperation</i> around 2001. I had just finished my time as an undergrad and was so excited to have time to read 'just for fun'. <br/><br/>What I remember from </span>
  <span id="freeText13473989351804289647" style="display:none"><b>**4.5-stars rounded up**</b><br><br>A bizarre cast of characters come together to fight an ancient and powerful entity of evil.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473169952ra/20420495.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That would be my single sentence synopsis if someone were to ask me, what is <i>Desperation</i> all about?<br><br>If you have ever read a Stephen King novel, however, you are probably aware that the real answer is <b>way more complex</b> than that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513055371ra/24658928.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I first read <i>Desperation</i> around 2001. I had just finished my time as an undergrad and was so excited to have time to read 'just for fun'. <br><br>What I remember from that initial read is that although I enjoyed the premise, I didn't really get it and I ultimately decided on a 3-star rating.<br><br>Now, close to 20-years later, this is pretty damn close to <u>a perfect read for me</u>!!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498702858ra/23153694.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What changed?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515241518ra/24844850.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not really sure. This time through I became invested very quickly. The characters were a huge part of the enjoyment factor for me. <br><br>King is a master of developing every aspect of a character's personality and their backstory. You never wonder what the motivation is.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524119680ra/25400178.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In my very humble opinion, no one does character development quite like the King. But a lot of it had to do with just settling into another one of his stories. <br><br>He has a very distinct style that is hella nostalgic for me; <b>it feels like home</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487968441ra/22069532.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Desperation</i> also has one of my all-time favorite tropes: a mix-matched group of characters, placed into extraordinary circumstances, who band together, no matter their differences, to fight against the forces of evil.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561417154ra/27720903.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Good versus Evil.<br><br>I love it. I'm here for it every damn time.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561417154ra/27720904.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This novel is extremely graphic with gore and violence on page. Some of the scenes made my toes curl and my stomach lurch. The use of creepy crawlers to instill fear was expertly crafted. <br><br>If this is not your thing, you may want to hard pass on this one. Otherwise, if you are a seasoned King, or general Horror reader, get ready to jump into a bloody brilliant good time! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561417154ra/27720905.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My one extremely slight critique would be that the final showdown felt a little rushed, hence the 4.5-star rating, as opposed to a full 5. <br><br>This book has a nice, long build-up, and I could definitely have read some more substance at the end. It was great, but still I wanted more!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466250431ra/19457787.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I am <b>beyond happy</b> that I took the plunge and reread this 706-page beast of modern Horror. <br><br>I am currently rereading <i>The Regulators</i> and digging the many connections I missed the first time around. <br><br><u>I would definitely recommend reading these two back-to-back for maximum enjoyment!</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561417154ra/27720902.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13473989351804289647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12709505337693633098"><b>Yikes!</b> U.S. 50 is much more than "the loneliest highway in America" when you end up in <b>DESPERATION!</b><p><b>It all begins</b> with a monstrosity of a 6' 7" police officer from <b>hell</b> and a scary trip into town for one unwary traveler after another; and once you do make it to town, well, the <b>deadly</b> creep-fest begins.</p><p>This chunkster of a novel is filled with <u>really</u> icky creepy crawlers, horrific & gruesome <b>death,</b> and enough blood and gore to fill a movie theatre, but when eleven year old David Carver enters the p</p></span>
  <span id="freeText12709505337693633098" style="display:none"><b>Yikes!</b> U.S. 50 is much more than "the loneliest highway in America" when you end up in <b>DESPERATION!</b><p><b>It all begins</b> with a monstrosity of a 6' 7" police officer from <b>hell</b> and a scary trip into town for one unwary traveler after another; and once you do make it to town, well, the <b>deadly</b> creep-fest begins.</p><p>This chunkster of a novel is filled with <u>really</u> icky creepy crawlers, horrific &amp; gruesome <b>death,</b> and enough blood and gore to fill a movie theatre, but when eleven year old David Carver enters the picture, <i>(and steals the show)</i> you'll also hear about friend Brian's miracle, a promise made to GOD and the power of prayer.</p><p>I admit it, this is one of those horror reads that made me want to scream at the characters <i>(more than once)</i> to get the hell out of dodge while the getting was good, but, of course, they don't......they prolong the reader's misery by waiting out a blustery sand storm <b>in the dark,</b> share scary stories of the supernatural <i>(while worrying about the "thing" outside) and then <u>still</u> enter the <b>evil</b> pit of hell! <b>Tak!</b></i></p><p> <b>Update: August 16, 2018 -</b> The movie version is super creepy too! It closely follows the novel with the GIANT sheriff setting up and terrorizing unsuspecting travelers and leading them to the desolate town of <b>DESPERATION</b> where dead bodies litter the streets. There's blood and gore as in the book.....and ewwww the evil presence!</p></span>

<div id="review_524904691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524904691" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/524904691?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=acquired-in-2013">acquired-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524904691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9466755236346306531">Why, what a splendid book. Gosh! <i>Tak.</i><br/><br/><i>”I see holes like eyes.”</i><br/><br/><i>Desperation</i> is one of the downright scariest books I’ve read, and the scares come early. King manages, for the most part, to keep the tension up throughout the novel, which makes it one hell of an uneasy read. Some sequences are somewhat bizarre, and others are bluntly offensive, although this is only what you’d expect from a novel such as this: it’s not meant to be easy reading after all. <br/><br/><i>Something about this bothered [him], but for n</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9466755236346306531" style="display:none">Why, what a splendid book. Gosh! <i>Tak.</i><br /><br /><i>”I see holes like eyes.”</i><br /><br /><i>Desperation</i> is one of the downright scariest books I’ve read, and the scares come early. King manages, for the most part, to keep the tension up throughout the novel, which makes it one hell of an uneasy read. Some sequences are somewhat bizarre, and others are bluntly offensive, although this is only what you’d expect from a novel such as this: it’s not meant to be easy reading after all. <br /><br /><i>Something about this bothered [him], but for now he paid no attention. His fright had grown into a sense of foreboding so strong and yet so diffuse that he felt a little as if he’d eaten something laced with poison.</i><br /><br />The story is definitely reminiscent of King’s earlier output and 1980s horror in general. Parallels can be drawn, not only with King’s own work, but also with novels like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19593.Floating_Dragon" title="Floating Dragon by Peter Straub" rel="nofollow noopener">Floating Dragon</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32435.Phantoms" title="Phantoms by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">Phantoms</a>. The nature of the supernatural antagonist is somewhat vague, but purposely so. Is it Demonic? Extraterrestrial? Biological?<br /><br /><i>Dolls with no little girls around to mind them were sort of creepy under any conditions, that was his opinion, at least, and to come upon one abandoned by the roadside, half-buried in blowing sand—</i><br /><br />It’s a visual novel, and King makes very effective use of imagery. The abandoned RV with its door banging in the wind, the doll by the roadside… it’s enough to raise hackles. The desert in this novel isn’t as much majestic as it is creepy in its desolation. And always menacing.<br /><br /><i>”Tell you what, pilgrim—this smells bad.”</i><br /><br />On the face of it, it’s typical King fare: very small town, multiple POV characters, supernatural evil, a healthy dose of Americana et al…. but <i>Desperation</i> does have one or two aces up its sleeve. It has some novelty value, having been released alongside <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10596.The_Regulators" title="The Regulators by Richard Bachman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Regulators</a>. It also has an epic and mythical sweep that can at least <i>partly</i> be attributed to the setting. Have I mentioned just how scary it gets?<br /><br /><i>“What’s that?” she whimpered. “Oh my God, what is it?”</i><br /><br />There is an overt religious theme present here and King tackles themes like the nature of God (“God is cruel.” Vs “God is love.”), the nature of Divine Intervention, and Redemption etc. Just how much of this will appeal to the reader would probably depend. I can’t speak for others, but I enjoyed the book. <br /><br /><i>”My head is full of blackbirds.”</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9466755236346306531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66215345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66215345" />
    <a title="Nicholas Armstrong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2593734-nicholas-armstrong"><img alt="Nicholas Armstrong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284413844p2/2593734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66215345?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicholas Armstrong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicholas Armstrong" href="/user/show/2593734-nicholas-armstrong">Nicholas Armstrong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66215345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16198535079997146831">I'm an indecisive rater and my rating on this will probably fluctuate with mood and memory but regardless of that this is a great read. <br/><br/>What I always found insulting was how easily critics, snobs, and pretentious twits write-off Stephen King because he writes stories about realistic people in fantastic situations. So what? Seriously, he writes amazingly so why give a damn what he writes about? Desperation is a perfect example of horror and fantastic writing and anyone who doesn't think so can go</span>
  <span id="freeText16198535079997146831" style="display:none">I'm an indecisive rater and my rating on this will probably fluctuate with mood and memory but regardless of that this is a great read. <br /><br />What I always found insulting was how easily critics, snobs, and pretentious twits write-off Stephen King because he writes stories about realistic people in fantastic situations. So what? Seriously, he writes amazingly so why give a damn what he writes about? Desperation is a perfect example of horror and fantastic writing and anyone who doesn't think so can go stick their nose in some classics of literature and sip wine and think about how superior they are.<br /><br />The first thing that gripped me in this book was how goddamn creepy it really was. There are few things that scare me, really, but cops are one of them. Cops scare me because I'm terrified of prison. I have no reason to go but dammit if I haven't read and seen things that have convinced me that sometimes innocent people get put away and horrible, horrible things happen to them. So the opening scenes of Desperation which show a sheriff who is seemingly innocent had me gripped and on the edge of my seat already. The characters were tense because of the bizarre way the cop pulls them over and the fact that they <i>do</i> have pot on them. This is probably my favorite part of the book but that does not mean it is the only good part. King's use of repetition of the senses here really astounded me. I never knew how powerful repetition could be until I read this book and this scene and I begin to sweat as hard as I thought the characters were. As their paranoia grew I could feel my own paranoia growing until I wanted to shout at the book "Are you a good guy? Is this going to turn out as horrible as it feels?" I don't know how many other authors use this method or have used it successfully but this was my first book that exhibited it noticeably and it blew me away. King's literary tools and knowledge of how to use them really awes me at times.<br /><br />From there the tension never slows and never stops. The characters are filled with real emotions, memories, and personalities. The woman (whose name I forget) is badass. Seriously, her and the writer were my two favorite characters, flaws and all.<br /><br />Yes, this is a horror. Yes, it is not filled with symbolism or a greater cultural message which we all probably know. Despite all of this it is still remarkably well-written and any author that makes me feel what the characters are feeling and the absolute hopelessness of a situation gets a thumbs up.<br /><br />Thumbs up King. Screw the snobs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16198535079997146831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_158686862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158686862" />
    <a title="Mari Biella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3895257-mari-biella"><img alt="Mari Biella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442624121p2/3895257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158686862?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mari Biella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mari Biella" href="/user/show/3895257-mari-biella">Mari Biella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3895257-mari-biella?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3895257-mari-biella?shelf=dark-fiction">dark-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3895257-mari-biella?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3895257-mari-biella?shelf=modern">modern</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3895257-mari-biella?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158686862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8249622625628398668">Say what you will about Stephen King, but you've got to hand it to our man in Maine: sitting down with one of his novels is never a struggle. Having read a number of his books, I've gradually come to think of him as being a bit like an old friend: a charming, chatty old friend who, for the price of a paperback, will happily sit down with you and tell you one of his numerous stories, stories whose occasional nastiness seems quite at odds with their mild-mannered narrator. On this level, <i>Desperati</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8249622625628398668" style="display:none">Say what you will about Stephen King, but you've got to hand it to our man in Maine: sitting down with one of his novels is never a struggle. Having read a number of his books, I've gradually come to think of him as being a bit like an old friend: a charming, chatty old friend who, for the price of a paperback, will happily sit down with you and tell you one of his numerous stories, stories whose occasional nastiness seems quite at odds with their mild-mannered narrator. On this level, <i>Desperation</i> does not disappoint; you're likely to be hooked from the very first page. And, yes, it really <i>is</i> pretty nasty – but then I have got a slight phobia of creepy little towns, so I would say that.<br /><br />Highway 50 in Nevada is apparently (being a Brit I'd hardly know) "The Loneliest Highway in America" – not the kind of place where you'd want to run out of petrol, have an accident or, indeed, meet a seemingly psychopathic policeman, as a random group of travellers are about to find out to their cost. In fact, the policeman is just the tip of the iceberg, as the actual source of the horror is something bigger, older and considerably more deadly than one man. The small mining town of Desperation, once a small but safe and friendly place, has been devastated by an ancient evil, and it falls to a ragged group of survivors to do battle with that evil. <br /><br />It's astounding how many of our primal fears King works on, and with what apparent ease: the fear of being possessed, the fear of bodily degeneration and decay, the dark, being alone, not being alone, wide open spaces, confined spaces, and of course what horrors might lurk in those spaces. In many ways this is not for the easily-upset: it's genuinely horrific on occasion, and most certainly gory. King was never the man to spare us sickening physical details, and he's on form here, disgusting us with every dribble of blood, every rotten lump of flesh and every putrid corpse. The foulness can get a bit much on occasion, and yes, it does begin to feel a bit gratuitous, but it's a compelling story, so you can overlook that.<br /><br />There are one or two gripes: as is so often the case with King, he starts off so well, and with such an intriguing premise, that he actually sort of writes himself into a corner; the ending is a disappointment, not to mention unintentionally mildly funny. And of course there are the recycled characters, the characters who have made numerous appearances in other King novels – the young boy with strange powers, the weary, cynical writer, the slightly downtrodden woman who has to struggle against the odds – but then again the fact that they keep coming back only really testifies to how successful they were to begin with. If ever a writer was a victim of his own success, it's SK; but then, in accordance with one of the major themes of the novel, God is cruel. Recommended, if not for the faint of heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8249622625628398668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50893023-johann-jobis89?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776882582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15076860711436826453">"In these silences something may rise."<br/><br/>What a book! What a ride! Tak!<br/><br/>This is a story about the little mining town of Desperation. Regulating the traffic on the nearby Route 50 is Collie Entragian, who is an absolutely giant madman. If you're caught with a license plate number missing or you've got a flat tire...tough luck. Collie brings passers-by into Desperation where the real nightmare begins.<br/><br/>I loved this book from beginning to end, I was hooked from the very first page. It's an apocalyptic d</span>
  <span id="freeText15076860711436826453" style="display:none">"In these silences something may rise."<br /><br />What a book! What a ride! Tak!<br /><br />This is a story about the little mining town of Desperation. Regulating the traffic on the nearby Route 50 is Collie Entragian, who is an absolutely giant madman. If you're caught with a license plate number missing or you've got a flat tire...tough luck. Collie brings passers-by into Desperation where the real nightmare begins.<br /><br />I loved this book from beginning to end, I was hooked from the very first page. It's an apocalyptic drama of God and evil, madness and revelation. There is a constant sense of tension that King holds over you relentlessly.<br /><br />It's true horror as the amount of gore and blood and guts is enough to last you for a lifetime. There's scary animals everywhere from coyotes to scorpions to buzzards to recluse spiders...with vivid imagery and descriptions. You could not wish for any more!<br /><br />People appear to have issues with the religious undertone of the book, but I personally enjoyed this aspect. I felt like it was necessary in order for this story to progress and make sense. It allowed for the character David Carver to really shine. A young boy with the weight of everyone's survival on his shoulders.<br /><br />The other characters were equally awesome. Steve and Cynthia...Johnny...the rest of the Carver family, Mary. King really developed each with their own unique characterisation and this is truly why he is the King.<br /><br />One of my top King books. An addictive read with a relentless pace.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6015493" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18059921735477752767">So, I dropped the pretention and read a Stephen King novel. True, I read several of King's works...in middle school...but I thought that it was time to give him another chance. After all, King's popularity is eclipsed only by, oh, I don't know...Jesus? Well, not Jesus...but someone popular.<br/><br/>I'll admit, the story was engaging. King has a way with propelling his story-lines over hundreds of pages without taking a breath. Or so it would seem. Unfortunately, the mediocrity of his prose is, at best, d</span>
  <span id="freeText18059921735477752767" style="display:none">So, I dropped the pretention and read a Stephen King novel. True, I read several of King's works...in middle school...but I thought that it was time to give him another chance. After all, King's popularity is eclipsed only by, oh, I don't know...Jesus? Well, not Jesus...but someone popular.<br /><br />I'll admit, the story was engaging. King has a way with propelling his story-lines over hundreds of pages without taking a breath. Or so it would seem. Unfortunately, the mediocrity of his prose is, at best, distracting and at worst infuriating. How many internal monologues can one author insert haphazardly into a single paragraph? I don't know, but King sure does: twenty-seven. Seriously though, King's writing suffers from a lack of ingenuity. Metaphors are ham-fisted and cliched, character development is superficial at best, and the dialogue is trite and unconvincing. The upshot to King's fast-paced, yet uninspired, novel? It only took a few hours to finish.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14932330628199720789"><br/><p>
  <strong>
    <em>“Dolls with no little girls around to mind them were sort of creepy under any conditions.” </em>
  </strong>
</p><br/><p>
  <em>Tak</em>
</p><br/><p>As a constant King reader, I was looking forward to diving into his twisted mindset again, for believe it or not this was my first King book this year and immediately from page one it felt like home. The whole setting for this book lends itself well to the extreme creepy factor from the ghost town in the middle of a desert to the long stretches of highway that just give this unsettling f</p></span>
  <span id="freeText14932330628199720789" style="display:none"><br><p>
  <strong>
    <em>“Dolls with no little girls around to mind them were sort of creepy under any conditions.” </em>
  </strong>
</p><br><p>
  <em>Tak</em>
</p><br><p>As a constant King reader, I was looking forward to diving into his twisted mindset again, for believe it or not this was my first King book this year and immediately from page one it felt like home. The whole setting for this book lends itself well to the extreme creepy factor from the ghost town in the middle of a desert to the long stretches of highway that just give this unsettling feeling like something bad is about happen.</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1503505817i/23669129._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image result for highway 50 nevada creepy gif" width="417" height="278" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>
  <strong>
    <em>“You said 'God is cruel' the way a person who's lived his whole life on Tahiti might say 'Snow is cold'. You </em>
    <em>knew</em>
    <em><strong>,</strong> but you didn't understand." He stepped close to David and put his palms on the boy's cold cheeks. "Do you know how cruel your God can be, David. How fantastically cruel?”</em>
  </strong>
</p><br>The plot revolves around this isolated town called <strong>Desperation</strong> which is located in Nevada, it seems deserted and the only inhabitant is the sheriff who patrols Highway 50 where a bunch of outsiders will, unfortunately, cross paths with the devil himself. Somehow, they get pulled over for some sort of technicality with the law and are brought to Desperation and all hell breaks loose.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503505817ra/23669130.gif" alt="Image result for all hell breaks loose office gif" width="229" height="159" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My experience reading this polarizing, before starting this I read that the book was too heavy on the religiousness or “preachy” and I was still not put off by that because <strong>The Stand</strong> also drew some inspiration from the Bible and used that to explore the Good vs Evil trope it was done smartly and the characters didn’t feel like biblical prophets but when it came to this book it felt like I was literally being talked down at. The plot was steady and the suspense was incredible as one would expect with a King but the second half the religious ideologies overtook the storyline.<br><p>
  <strong>
    <em>“In these silences, something may rise” </em>
  </strong>
</p><br>The characters had a similar effect with the plot, at the beginning each individual had such a strong presence but they slowly dwindled… The whole idea of free will in regards to religion was touched on but once the characters started losing their own personal belief and started making really dumb decisions my enjoyment level started plummeting.<br><br>Apart from all that the book is really fast paced, devouring the 700pages in a weeks time and the gore factor was top notch. <em>Exploring addiction and alcoholism was well done as the subject hits close to home for Stephen King</em>. I would definitely still recommend it for the sharp writing and atmosphere but it isn’t like my favorite King book, I have read better. Still, you sound check it out if the premise sounds interesting or if you are King addict.<br><p>I would definitely check out The Regulators to see how the narratives pair together.</p><br><p>Have you read it what are your thoughts on it?</p><br><br>___________________________________________________<br><b> Really conflicted about this I need to get thoughts my order </b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503074056ra/23626549.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14932330628199720789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3397702547324540396">While there is no doubt Stephen King is a great author with an incredible ability to write, he still needs an editor. Obviously, no one bothered to edit this novel from way, way, way, way, way, way, way, way, way, way too long. Are King’s editors too intimidated to do their jobs? It certainly appears so in this exceedingly unnecessarily long wordy work. Not even close to his best work. 2 out of 10 stars for this never ending yarn.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2989124636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2989124636" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2989124636?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340952658" href="/book/show/1020712.Desperation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2989124636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17221275187411723292">What I learned from this book: tall people are The Devil. *lol*<br/><br/>This was … not the most excellent King I’ve read so far, but pretty good nonetheless.<br/><br/>There are four groups of people: a young couple (Mary and Peter Jackson), a family of four (father, mother, an 11-year-old boy and his younger sister), a washed-up writer, the writer’s assistant (who has to follow him at a little distance while his boss is crossing the USofA on his motorcycle) and a hitchhiker he’s picked up not too long ago.<br/>These fo</span>
  <span id="freeText17221275187411723292" style="display:none">What I learned from this book: tall people are The Devil. *lol*<br /><br />This was … not the most excellent King I’ve read so far, but pretty good nonetheless.<br /><br />There are four groups of people: a young couple (Mary and Peter Jackson), a family of four (father, mother, an 11-year-old boy and his younger sister), a washed-up writer, the writer’s assistant (who has to follow him at a little distance while his boss is crossing the USofA on his motorcycle) and a hitchhiker he’s picked up not too long ago.<br />These four groups have one thing in common: they are each either stopped by a cop out on the highway or are connected to the people who have been arrested and thus end up in the small town of Desperation.<br /><br />The problem is that there is something profoundly wrong with the cop. From supposedly planted weed, to eerie phrases that steal into his speech pattern, unnerving the people he’s talking to. <br />Also unnerving is the fact that the town is empty. From the recently re-opened mines to the main street. Not a soul to be seen.<br />And here’s a third unnerving fact: the animals (from coyotes to buzzards and scorpions) seem to have been instrumentalized too.<br />But why / how?<br /><br />Well, that is exactly what the people are trying to find out after shit hits the fan and they realize they’ve pretty much landed in hell.<br /><br />One thing I was definitely not into was the whole religion schtick. I know King isn’t religious himself, so that makes it a little better, but the pious message is strong in this one (or King’s sarcasm is too weak here). I honestly hoped <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[David would die, preferably while praying, realizing in the last few seconds of his life that it was all just his imagination <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Alas.<br /><br />For those of you who are reading Stephen King, regularly even, this will be one of those rewarding stories that have some slight connection to others, telling us of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[children with powers like Danny in <i>The Shining</i> and yet another hole in the fabric of our reality that let in <i>something</i> - Pennywise was such a thing, the mist in the novella of the same name was basically a curtain drawn back as well, … <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />I really liked the atmosphere in the little town, when we didn’t know quite what was wrong though we could already be sure that something was VERY wrong indeed. The origin story itself was cool as well though how they found out … I don’t know. Not to mention that I hated all the instrumentalized animals <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and that they had to die <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Like I said, very enjoyable, but not King’s best. <br />By the way, my audiobook was narrated by King himself and let me tell you: the man is a darn good audiobook narrator!<br /><br /><br />P.S.: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was September 21st when the miners accidentally freed Tak from its underground prison, thus unleashing evil upon the world ... my sister was born on September 21st ... IT EXPLAINS EVERYTHING! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="17221275187411723292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_600511589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600511589" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600511589?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670868360" href="/book/show/441239.Desperation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600511589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15819141795616880508">The first time I read <i>Desperation</i>, I read it back to back with <i>The Regulators</i> in the fall 1996. Had I been reviewing in my teenage years, I probably would have given this two stars, and <i>The Regulators</i> four stars. The latter is a fun book from beginning to end, while <i>Desperation</i> takes off like a crackhead escaping police custody only to run out of steam about halfway to the sanctuary of his crack den. Sad Panda. <br/><br/>This read was a little bit better than the first because I was expecting the slow-as-</span>
  <span id="freeText15819141795616880508" style="display:none">The first time I read <i>Desperation</i>, I read it back to back with <i>The Regulators</i> in the fall 1996. Had I been reviewing in my teenage years, I probably would have given this two stars, and <i>The Regulators</i> four stars. The latter is a fun book from beginning to end, while <i>Desperation</i> takes off like a crackhead escaping police custody only to run out of steam about halfway to the sanctuary of his crack den. Sad Panda. <br /><br />This read was a little bit better than the first because I was expecting the slow-as-mud, worship-ridden final 300 pages, so I'm giving it another star. Most of my problems with this book is personal. The God angle leaves a bad taste in my mouth. I'm not a religious person, and for the most part, I don't get along with religious persons. I'm too fucking opinionated, and I'm notorious for flapping my jaws. Mostly because these are the people who laugh at me for believing in Santa Claus until I was 13 and don't see the irony in having a laugh at the hopeful child I once was. You can have your Land of Make-Believe, I have my own. So yeah, the Come to Jesus Parade isn't to my liking. Purely subjective. If you're rollin' holy, this is probably the King book for you.<br /><br />Oh, and... Diablo Mine? Stephen, if you thought you were being subtle with the subtext, you failed. <i>Tak!</i><br /><br /><i>Desperation</i> is probably the closest thing to a horror novel King had written since <i>Needful Things</i>, which was... seven books back, I think. In between you had books like <i>Gerald's Game, Dolores Claiborne, The Green Mile, Rose Madder</i>... you know, stuff like that. Not one of those books are what horror fans would call scary. They scared me, but I'm fucking strange. <i>Desperation</i> was a return to such balls-out terrors. You have a psycho cop who's not everything he seems. You have animals and the nastiest of insect life acting strangely. A haunted mine. Statues that make you wanna fuck people to death. You know, Disney type of shit. My point is, this book is brutal, and I loved that aspect. <br /><br />Oddly enough, a miniscule - and I mean teensy-tiny - side character from <i>Rose Madder</i> has a pretty substantial role in this book. That one still shocks me. I know full and well some characters come into our lives and refuse to leave, but I remember thinking and <i>still</i> think Cynthia was the last person I expected to see within these pages. My favorite character above any other is Johnny Marinville, though. One of King's best characters, that one.<br /><br />For tie-ins to the King-verse, click view spoiler, but please expect spoilers for <b>ALL</b> of King's work and not just this novel. Thank you.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Obvious Tie-ins:<br />Daughters and Sisters, Norman Daniels, Cynthia Smith (<i>Rose Madder</i>).<br />The mine and quonset huts from <i>Wolves of the Calla</i>.<br />Someone mentions <i>Misery in Paradise</i>, which is a romance novel written by Paul Sheldon. This also ties <i>Misery</i> deeper into the Dark Tower and King-verse. <i>Tak!</i><br /><br />Conspiracy Theories:<br />I find it strange that King used the Mr. Smiley on the bag of weed in <i>Desperation</i>, and then used it again <b>TWO DECADES LATER</b> in <i>Mr. Mercedes</i>. I've been trying to six-degrees <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> into the rest of the King-verse since I read the book almost a year ago and I've been coming up empty. There are mentions of the movie adaptation for <i>Carrie</i> and <i>IT</i>, but nothing stating that <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> is part of the same universe. <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> seems to be set in "the real world" apart from the King-verse, so I don't know if I'm grasping at straws or if he really did use Mr Smiley to tie <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> into the Dark Tower. I know the bad guy's name in <i>Revival</i> comes up to 19 letters, so we have that... but <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> still elludes me. I guess we'll see if I can find anything in <i>Finders Keepers</i> this June. <i>Tak!</i><br /><br />Also, dig on this, friends and neighbors...<br /><br />What if the wendigo from <i>Pet Sematary</i> is the same kind of demon as Tak. And what if both of these bad boys are from the Prim, that chaotic void referenced in the Dark Tower books? Aw yeah, kids, I think they are.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In summation: <i>Desperation</i> is a fun ride for about 350 pages before taking a detour into Bible Country for the final 300 pages. If you're cool with that, you'll probably dig this battle between good and evil accessed by way of the loneliest highway in America. <br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Is that a shotgun shell in your pocket or are you happy to have found Jesus?</b><br /><br />(P.S. I won't be rereading <i>The Regulators</i> next. I know it sounds strange, but it's technically NOT a King novel. Yes, I know he's Richard Bachman too, you're not telling me anything I don't already know, but it's not MEANT to be a King book. I have my reasons, and I will explain them eventually. Promise.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15819141795616880508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1673697831562637437">While so much of modern (and not so modern) horror is filled with religious terror, that unholy flipside to the noumen, there will always be a subset of horror devoted to scratching out particular aspects of it and developing it.<br/><br/>So, rather than going all tentacle monsters, we get down to the heart of the matter and terrify ourselves by saying that ALL is horror. :) Maybe it doesn't make for the most spectacular action tale, but it certainly bites you in the ass after a good long read. <br/><br/>Wait... di</span>
  <span id="freeText1673697831562637437" style="display:none">While so much of modern (and not so modern) horror is filled with religious terror, that unholy flipside to the noumen, there will always be a subset of horror devoted to scratching out particular aspects of it and developing it.<br /><br />So, rather than going all tentacle monsters, we get down to the heart of the matter and terrify ourselves by saying that ALL is horror. :) Maybe it doesn't make for the most spectacular action tale, but it certainly bites you in the ass after a good long read. <br /><br />Wait... did I just say this book doesn't have tentacular horrors from the vicinity of the Red King? Oh, sorry, no, this absolutely does. The beastie is beautiful. And the plot? It's everything you might want in a spaghetti western so long as you don't mind massive (and good) flashback-like sequences that give us the full story of this little town of Desperation. <br /><br />Honesty time.<br /><br />It was good but not quite as good as MOST of King. I always prefer his big supernatural bits in general, but not all of them are even in their quality. I grew bored with bits of this even tho, ostensibly, there wasn't really a REAL slow moment in it.<br /><br />Maybe I just didn't care for the whole surface religious aspect (as opposed to crazy nutjob religious characters or a big twist on the source of the holy) even though, in the end, I am forced to think. The rest of it got a bit annoying.<br /><br />But Good News, ye Faithful! I think you will find that this particular horror will suit your needs quite well!</span>

  <span id="freeText16581320952126032146" style="display:none">UUUUUUUUUUGGGHHHH I FEEL SO BETRAYED BY THIS DUMB BOOK.<br /><br />The first half, maybe even two thirds and I was all HEY THIS MIGHT BE MY FAVORITE KING NOVEL. <div id="review_2659549086" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2659549086" />
    <a title="Sheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/91276499-sheri"><img alt="Sheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546105491p2/91276499.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2659549086?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheri" href="/user/show/91276499-sheri">Sheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670868360" href="/book/show/441239.Desperation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/91276499-sheri?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/91276499-sheri?shelf=horror-scary-creepy">horror-scary-creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/91276499-sheri?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2659549086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15226677215603425280">I really enjoyed this book. There was not one part of the story where I felt I wanted to pause or put it down. It's the type of story that makes me appreciate the talent that goes into writing. <br/>The story is one that has been told been many times before. There are a group of people that do not know one another that are thrown together by chance and fighting together to survive the villain. <br/>The book is ALL Stephen King as he's loved by his fans, from first page to the last page. I can honestly say</span>
  <span id="freeText15226677215603425280" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. There was not one part of the story where I felt I wanted to pause or put it down. It's the type of story that makes me appreciate the talent that goes into writing. <br />The story is one that has been told been many times before. There are a group of people that do not know one another that are thrown together by chance and fighting together to survive the villain. <br />The book is ALL Stephen King as he's loved by his fans, from first page to the last page. I can honestly say that there were some details that made my jaw drop. It will always amaze me how an author can take small, seemingly meaningless clues, and introduce them at the beginning of the story and somehow that one item works it's way into the closing scene. I'm also amazed at how Stephen King has interwoven all of the books he's ever written. There are people, places, and things that show up in one book and then surprisingly you find them in another book. Every book/story is connected. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15226677215603425280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1883174384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883174384" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883174384?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670868360" href="/book/show/441239.Desperation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883174384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12423339362194754553">Here we have it, folks: the biggest shock yet in the Stephen King reread. <br/><br/>Before today, I considered <i>Desperation</i> bottom-of-the-barrel King. Desperate King. I felt the religiosity was blatant, tasteless; the story derivative of things King had done better before. Funny how our tastes evolve and change as we get older, isn’t it? My sole reading of this novel was in my sophomore year of high school — about six years’ worth of stuff has happened to me since then. What can I say, I was able to apprec</span>
  <span id="freeText12423339362194754553" style="display:none">Here we have it, folks: the biggest shock yet in the Stephen King reread. <br /><br />Before today, I considered <i>Desperation</i> bottom-of-the-barrel King. Desperate King. I felt the religiosity was blatant, tasteless; the story derivative of things King had done better before. Funny how our tastes evolve and change as we get older, isn’t it? My sole reading of this novel was in my sophomore year of high school — about six years’ worth of stuff has happened to me since then. What can I say, I was able to appreciate this epic, apocalyptic tale—King’s take on the book of Revelation, so to speak.<br /><br />What I didn’t pick up on before is just how visceral and gruesome <i>Desperation</i> is: King gleefully rips and mangles his characters in ways not seen since his early years. What this makes for is a novel that, while sometimes overly pretentious in its theological posturing, is packed to the brim with scene after scene of gleeful, demonic, sexual terror. This is perhaps the one and only time a King novel reads like Clive Barker, albeit with more doses of Jesus and Americana than Barker has ever gone for. <br /><br />I have to say it, though . . . I don’t like David. Nope. Kid suffers from Mother Abagail Syndrome: a supposed prophet of God, he comes off as pompous and grating in his assuredness. Even after what happens to him during the course of the story, I can’t muster up any sympathy for him. From him comes this novel’s most frustrating religious elements (the sardines and crackers scene— *rolls eyes into the back of my head*) and I’m just not here for it.<br /><br />Like <i>The Dark Half</i> and <i>Firestarter</i> before it, rereading this novel made me appreciate the work and see what it is others see. While certainly not perfect, this is one of Stephen King’s most unsettling and provocative works. If one is looking for scares, he or she could do much worse. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12423339362194754553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2600467340" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2600467340" />
    <a title="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9722719-chandra-claypool-wherethereadergrows"><img alt="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534358832p2/9722719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2600467340?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" href="/user/show/9722719-chandra-claypool-wherethereadergrows">Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501192234" href="/book/show/36334232-desperation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2600467340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1892695305420832390">Ah Desperation! So good to reread you again. It has been around 20 years since I've read this book and while I still prefer this over The Regulators, I didn't <i>quite</i> enjoy it as much as I have in my first round. You certainly can't take away from King's ability to weave a tale, insert gore, religion, faith, horror and bloody ooziness into one solid crazy ass novel.<br/><br/>Some people have issues with the religious aspect of this book. I am not a religious person by any means but this never really bothers</span>
  <span id="freeText1892695305420832390" style="display:none">Ah Desperation! So good to reread you again. It has been around 20 years since I've read this book and while I still prefer this over The Regulators, I didn't <i>quite</i> enjoy it as much as I have in my first round. You certainly can't take away from King's ability to weave a tale, insert gore, religion, faith, horror and bloody ooziness into one solid crazy ass novel.<br /><br />Some people have issues with the religious aspect of this book. I am not a religious person by any means but this never really bothers me when reading books, especially horror books as this can be seen quite a bit with the whole good vs. evil aspect that's a common theme. Some aren't as blatant about it as Desperation is, but it's still there. I still put it all in a fiction category and enjoy the read for what (I think) it's mean to be.<br /><br />While I did enjoy The Regulators a bit more my second time around, Desperation still holds its place in my heart between the two. Why? Well, we get more background on each of the characters, a more defined and "mature" Tak and a more developed story over all. (Not gonna lie though, I did miss the "fun" aspect of the Motocops though).<br /><br />I don't believe either of these books gets enough love. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="1892695305420832390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28670321" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28670321?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670868360" href="/book/show/441239.Desperation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=religion-y">religion-y</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28670321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6368040502463096207">This is probably the 4th or 5th time that I've read this book. I have always liked this story, although not as much as it's other half, <i>The Regulators</i>, but I have to say that this time, unfortunately, <i>Desperation</i> lost a little something for me. I actually downgraded it from a 4 star to a 3 star rating (OK, 3 1/2 maybe). <br/><br/>Maybe this is due to the fact that I'm on something of a King kick, and I've been reading a lot of his stuff within the past few months. I think, because of this, some of his les</span>
  <span id="freeText6368040502463096207" style="display:none">This is probably the 4th or 5th time that I've read this book. I have always liked this story, although not as much as it's other half, <i>The Regulators</i>, but I have to say that this time, unfortunately, <i>Desperation</i> lost a little something for me. I actually downgraded it from a 4 star to a 3 star rating (OK, 3 1/2 maybe). <br /><br />Maybe this is due to the fact that I'm on something of a King kick, and I've been reading a lot of his stuff within the past few months. I think, because of this, some of his less endearing (to me) writing tics show up, frequently, and wearing bright yellow LOOK AT ME! t-shirts. Maybe it's also that I'm a different reader than I used to be. I don't know. I still enjoyed the story, but I definitely did not love it as much as I used to. <br /><br />The main story centers around a group of people all brought into the town of Desperation by a cop on a rampage. They are stopped, seemingly at random, and arrested and held, and all around them the world has gone crazy. The inhabitants of the town have all been murdered. Animals act very un-animalistically, insects and spiders and snakes and birds and just about everything else that can be found in the desert all seem to be at the beck and call of some ancient being that has escaped... <br /><br />I love the idea of Tak, and the idea of the can tahs (little gods), and the effect that they have on people. I wish, this time around, that there was a little more history behind this aspect of the story. I also wished for a little more history of the first encounter. Granted, we definitely got more here than we did in, say, Pet Sematary. The evil origins of the burial ground are hinted at there, and that's all. But that's a different story, and here, the evil is a focal point of this story. Or rather the battle between good and evil. <br /><br />Which brings me to my next point. There is a large, large focus in this book on religion and faith and God. I'm not a religious person, but I don't mind when King writes about it, simply because I don't feel like he's taking a position of "I'm right and you're wrong if you don't see things my way." Even here, where he pretty much writes that God not only exists but sets about proving it for his characters, it doesn't feel... preachy. Or offensive. It's a "take it or leave it" proof, and unlike some other authors who write about God, King doesn't ram his beliefs down our throats. <br /><br />There's also an environmental statement thrown in there, although again King doesn't come right out and start lambasting anyone. He shows how mining can be bad -- very, very, bad -- but also how it can be necessary. Personally, being a liberalish kind of girl, I think that it does far more harm than good, but this isn't the time for another of my rants. You're welcome. ;) But one can view Tak as a kind of argument against digging and digging and pushing too far - you just never know what the dangers are. The can tahs can be seen as greed and want at any cost personified... if one chooses to interpret them that way. <br /><br />This book is also a prime example of how King's characters all seem to be very in tune with themselves and with their instincts. Far more in tune with whatever it is than I am. This is cool, but it's annoying as hell when he works it into the dialogue, because it comes out as a kind of statement/question, as if they are feeling something, but aren't quite sure, so they'd just better confirm. <br />Take for instance these examples: <br /><i>"You're going to the truck, aren't you?"<br />"You heard that, didn't you?"<br />"I'm going crazy, aren't I? <br />"We're all going to die, aren't we?"<br />"You're being sarcastic, aren't you?"</i><br />I could keep going, but I think you get the point. I just wish that someone would say something definitively and stick to it. If they are wrong, they are wrong, but questioning every statement gets on my nerves! Or at least ask a proper question. <br /><i>"Are we going to die?" <br />"Am I going crazy?" <br />"Did you hear that?" </i><br />There, not annoying. :)<br /><br />Overall, I liked the story, but I can't say that I got the same pleasure out of it this time around as I have in the past. The characters are real, real enough to be hateful sometimes, and the story itself is very good, but I can't say it's a favorite. <br /><br />On to <i>The Regulators</i>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6368040502463096207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
